chain management, material science, computational biology**, and much
else]{.underline} besides. [We're]{.underline} way [past]{.underline}
the [steam engines]{.underline} that Marx was sketching in his
notebooks.39 Is it not possible, then, that there have been sufficient
transformations in the forces of production to break out of the fetters
of a strictly capitalist mode of production? There are two versions of
this question. One is looking for a theological justification for this
appearance of something new as finally putting an end to the more
troubling aspects of capitalism for vectoralist class apologetics. But
the more salient version of the question might be to [ask whether what
has emerged]{.underline}, in addition to and laminated on top of a
capitalist mode of production, [is something]{.underline} qualitatively
[different]{.underline}, but [which generates new forms of class
domination]{.underline}, new forms of the extraction of surplus, even
new kinds of class formation. The emergence of [information as a

[might escape the confines of existing relations of production
and]{.underline} that it could [negate existing property
forms]{.underline}. (I return to this topic in Chapter 4). It looked for
a while as though [the one thing that]{.underline} really [could form
the basis of the commons was information]{.underline}. [It blew apart
the]{.underline} old [culture industry]{.underline}. Producers of
information started to think not just about their craft or trade
interests but about a class interest. Or so it looked early in the
twenty-first century when I wrote A Hacker Manifesto. What I did not
anticipate was the emergence of a whole other technique for the capture

want to confine creation within ever stricter forms of private property,
some took the opposite tack. [Rather than police or restrict free

[was to move its capture to a]{.underline} more [abstract

**need not**]{.underline} even [**be paid**, and the aggregate value of

**[monetized]{.underline}**.40 [This]{.underline} [new]{.underline} kind

[surplus value so much as **exploit an asymmetry of

get that]{.underline} [little]{.underline} piece of
[information]{.underline}, **[this ruling class gets all of that

exploits the asymmetry between the little you know and the aggregate it
knows]{.underline}**---an aggregate it collects [based on information
you were]{.underline} [obliged to "volunteer]{.underline}." In practice,
[this]{.underline} emergent [ruling class]{.underline} of our time
[insists on the confinement of]{.underline} particular acts of [creation
within the property form and access to collective creative
activity]{.underline}, [from which to harvest information]{.underline}
in the aggregate. [This is the vectoralist class.]{.underline} If the
capitalist class owns the means of production, **[the vectoralist class
owns the vectors of information]{.underline}**. They own the extensive
[vectors of **communication**]{.underline}, which **[traverse
space]{.underline}**. They own the intensive [vectors of
**computation**,]{.underline} which **[accelerate time]{.underline}**.
They own the **[copyrights]{.underline}**, the [**patents**,
and]{.underline} the **[trademarks]{.underline}** that
**[capture]{.underline}** attention or assign
**[ownership]{.underline}** to novel techniques. They own the

and monitor [the disposition and movement of any resource]{.underline}.
They own the [financial instruments that stand in for]{.underline} the
[value]{.underline} of every resource and that can be put out on markets
to crowdsource the possible value of every possible future combination
of those resources. They own [the algorithms that rank and
sort]{.underline} and assign particular [information]{.underline} in
particular circumstances. [This **vectoralist class comes to
dominate**]{.underline} [not just subordinate classes, but]{.underline}
**[other ruling classes as well]{.underline}**. Just as capital came to
dominate landed property, subsuming its control over land in a more
abstract and fungible property form, so too [the vectoralist class has
**subsumed and outflanked capital**]{.underline} in a more abstract
form. The capitalist class finds itself at a disadvantage. [Owning the
means of production]{.underline}, labor materialized into capital in the
sense of plant and equipment, [is]{.underline} a [rigid and
long-term]{.underline} investment. [Owning]{.underline} and controlling
[the vector]{.underline}, the hack of new information materialized into
patents, copyrights, brands, proprietary logistics. It [is more
abstract, flexible, adaptive]{.underline}. It is not more rational, but
it is more abstract. The vectoralist class monopolizes the crossroads
where information traffics, feeding like Michel Serres's parasite on the
buzz of information and noise at crucial junctures.42 The most obvious
aspect of vectoral rule in everyday life is its monopoly of attention,
although it is not reducible to this. As Yves Citton notes,
[in]{.underline} a world awash in [digital data]{.underline}, [what is
rare is]{.underline} the [attention]{.underline} paid to it.43
[**Commanding attention** through the ownership and control of brands,
celebrities and media "properties" is the]{.underline} public face, the
[**disintegrating spectacle,** of vectoral economy.]{.underline} 44 In
part, [this descends from]{.underline} what was formerly [the culture
industry]{.underline}. [But]{.underline} it is [no longer an industry
apart, commodified leisure. It's now integrated into the whole of
production and consumption.]{.underline} This brief sketch of the
supersession of capitalism as a dominant mode has the advantage of
enabling many of the features of contemporary life that are often
treated as separate to appear as aspects of the same historical
development. [The **rise of technology, financialization, neoliberalism,
and biopolitics** appear as **effects of the same transformation** of
the forces of production]{.underline}, putting pressure on the relations
of production, to the point where what bursts forth is a new ruling
class formation. In the usual historical narrative, [by the end of the
seventies]{.underline}, the forces of [labor]{.underline} had [fought
capital to a standstill]{.underline} in the overdeveloped world.45 In
this story, [financialization and neoliberalism come to the rescue.
**But how**?]{.underline} [**What** material means **made
financialization** even **possible**]{.underline}? What underlying
social forces enabled neoliberal ideas to even appear plausible as
policy instruments? [Why does this **coincide with the**]{.underline}
apparent **[birth of "tech"]{.underline}** as an
**[industry]{.underline}** sector? In the thought experiment I am
sketching, all of [these developments fit together]{.underline} in a
novel way. [The capitalist class was searching for a way out of
the]{.underline} impasse of confronting the [demands of
labor]{.underline} at a time when improvements of the old means of
production no longer yielded much by way of a productivity increase.
[The capitalist class]{.underline} thought it [found a way out by
**replacing labor with the vector**]{.underline} and escaping along it.
**[Globalization, deindustrialization, and outsourcing]{.underline}**
would [enable]{.underline} it [to be **free from the power of labor to

information [vector]{.underline} [would enable]{.underline} not just a
more abstract and flexible kind of production, but also of
[consumption]{.underline}, [through the financialization of everyday
life]{.underline}.46 Workers as producers found their jobs had moved
elsewhere; [workers as consumers found their purchasing power
restored]{.underline}--- at least [temporarily]{.underline}. **[Here's
the twist]{.underline}**: [what]{.underline} at first [appeared to
assist capital to defeat labor]{.underline} in the overdeveloped world
[was]{.underline} also **[a defeat for capital]{.underline}**. The
[novel]{.underline} forces of [production]{.underline} that enabled this

[dominant]{.underline} forces of production. [Power over the value chain
moves]{.underline} from the ownership and control of the means of
production [to ownership and control of the vectors]{.underline} of
information. Whole new industries arose, as did whole new
corporations---the so-called tech sector. But actually [**all
corporations** become]{.underline} increasingly **[organized
around]{.underline}** the ownership and control of
**[information]{.underline}**. [Control over]{.underline} the value
chain through ownership of the [information]{.underline} vector
[extends]{.underline} even **[into life itself]{.underline}**. This is
not the least reason, incidentally, [that it is no longer helpful to
posit the vitalism of living labor against capital as dead
labor]{.underline}. 47 [Not capital but **the vector enters the flesh**
and commands it]{.underline}, and not just as meat, but also **[as
information]{.underline}**, [through **monitoring**]{.underline} its
states, through **[modifying]{.underline}** its functions [with
drugs]{.underline} that alter chemical signals, through [**patenting**
aspects of life as design]{.underline}.48 [What is at stake is neither a
bios nor a polis but a regime of property in information extending into
the organism]{.underline}. [The novel forces of production]{.underline}
as they have emerged in our time [are]{.underline} [also forces of
reproduction]{.underline} [and]{.underline} forces of
[circulation]{.underline}. [The power of the vectoralist class is
not]{.underline} [cognitive]{.underline}; [nor]{.underline} is it a
power over the general [intellect]{.underline}.49 [It
thrives]{.underline} just as well [on noise]{.underline}, on
volatility[, on bad information as it does on]{.underline} any kind of
[intelligence or reason]{.underline}.50 [It reaches]{.underline} just as
[far into]{.underline} the [corporeality and]{.underline} even
[sexuality]{.underline} of the human as it does into the intellect.51
[The]{.underline} forms of [**artificial computational order** it is
creating are **not extensions or imitations of human cognition** but
**something else entirely**]{.underline}. 52 [One **cannot interpret**
the]{.underline} strangeness of this mode of [production
**using**]{.underline} the received **[hermeneutic conceptual
categories]{.underline}**, derived as they are [from a critique of the
relations of production of nineteenth-century steam-powered
capitalism]{.underline}. Indeed, one sees now how incomplete Marx's
critique was and remains. Even his critical understanding of capitalism
is still thinking capitalism metaphorically as like a giant,
dysfunctional steam engine, set to blow at any moment from unregulated
internal pressures.53 **[Marx is not able to think critically about
information]{.underline}** in the contemporary sense of the concept
because it is not one that the forces of production of his time have yet
produced. Marx found what was absent in the theories of Capital in his
time. He lifted the veil between exchange and production and found the
exploited labor that makes it. He wrote the heresy that Capital is dead
labor--- congealed pink goo---and he went on to write from the point of
view of the labor that capital exploits. So: [let's go looking for what
is absent in]{.underline} theories of both [Capital and
information]{.underline} in our time. Let's find [that peculiar class
who own and control information]{.underline}. Let's find [the exploited
class or classes that make it and are subjected to it]{.underline}. In
vulgar terms: [the capitalist class eats our bodies, **the vectoralist
class eats our brains**]{.underline}. Returning this thought experiment
to the present, one might then be able to think the historical
specificity of the contemporary moment. This, after all, was
[Marx's]{.underline} great achievement. He [thought his
moment]{.underline}. His present did not look to him like his past. It
had novel features that called into being concepts adequate to the
situation. Which leaves us with the paradoxical and provocative thought
that [any theory in which **the present appears as**]{.underline} in
essence [the same]{.underline} as the past of **[Marx's
time]{.underline}**, only different in a few matters of appearance,
**[can't]{.underline}** really **[be]{.underline}** a
"**[Marxist]{.underline}**" one, as [such fidelity is]{.underline}
necessarily [a betrayal of his achievement]{.underline}. Debord: "And
**[theories are made to die in the war of time]{.underline}**."54
Perhaps [we can **leave**]{.underline} such **[theological questions to
the faithful]{.underline}**, who are in any case an embattled and
diminished band. [Instead]{.underline}, here is a research agenda: [what
are the **current forces of production**]{.underline}, and how can they
be understood (in a preliminary way) under a modest set of concepts?
[How do those]{.underline} forces of production [give rise to
contemporary forms of class power]{.underline}, and [how has that
power]{.underline} in turn [shaped]{.underline} the particular form
[those forces of production]{.underline} have taken? [At what points
might the subordinate classes,]{.underline} obliged to live within the
world those forces of production make in the interests of those ruling
class, [be able to assert agency]{.underline} and autonomy? **[What
other world is still possible]{.underline}**, given the damage this
general economy has done to the world, with the means that it has
hitherto developed?55

#### The rationalization of information has created a new class relation -- power comes from surveillance and quantification. We sit in desks and fill in excel documents for hours under the guise of 'technical freedom', our information commodified. As long as the vector is owned by the few, propped up by both sides who attempt to analyze and justify using the outdated language of marx, the system won't change. 

**Wark 19** (McKenzie Wark, Activist, Writer, PhD in Communications,
Professor at the New School for Social Research and Eugene Lang College,
Culture and Media; Program Director, Gender Studies, 2019, Verso,
\"Capital is dead\", Chapter 4: The Class Location Blues)//gideon \*\[\]
= fixed typo

My question here would be: [why would one think, if this has already
given rise to more than one kind of rationalization of class antagonism
that overlapped and interfered with each other, that it would not give
rise to another]{.underline}? [The farmer--landlord antagonism arose out
of]{.underline} the antagonism between [serfs and the
nobility]{.underline}. 26 Serfs lost their lands by force or debt and
fled to the cities, while a rationalization of agricultural production
led to the expansion of a surplus that might feed urban populations, who
would become urban workers, in an antagonistic relation to capitalists.
And [yet landlords and capitalists]{.underline} also had interests that
[contradicted each other]{.underline}. But did rationalization stop,
with the creation of classes of farmer and worker? [What happens when
the **production**]{.underline}, not of food or products, but **[of new
information itself becomes rationalized]{.underline}**? Weber did not
have a lot to say about labor, but where he did, it was in terms of work
discipline. Employers are free to hire and fire. Workers lack ownership,
but workers are responsible for their own social reproduction. These are
the conditions under which indirect compulsion operates. But it raises
the problem of how to get maximum labor effort. Wright: "running
throughout Weber's work is the view that rationalization has perverse
effects that systematically threaten human dignity and welfare."27 But
Weber does not integrate interest in labor discipline and domination
into the category of class. Here we need a bit of Marx, for whom, as
Wright says, "exploitation infuses class analysis with a specific kind
of normative concern."28 Exploitation steers research to questions of
class as relational in both exchange and production. "Weber's treatment
of work effort as primarily a problem of economic rationality directs
class analysis towards a set of normative concerns centered above all on
the interests of capitalists: efficiency and rationalization."29
Wright's synthesis of Marx and Weber makes exploitation fundamental even
as it makes particular use of the idea of opportunity hoarding as that
which defines the "middle class." From there one could build up a
picture of [the United States as highly polarized by
exploitation]{.underline}, a country where [middle class opportunity
hoarding is being eroded by]{.underline} what he calls [neoliberalism
and deindustrialization]{.underline}. I think this can be understood
more clearly in terms of [new forces of production]{.underline} that
[instrumentalize and rationalize information]{.underline}, [giving rise
to new property forms and]{.underline} hence [new class
relations]{.underline}, [including an **antagonistic relation between a
hacker class tasked with making novelty out of
information**]{.underline} (the condition of it becoming property)
**[and a vectoralist class that owns or controls the vector of
information control and domination itself]{.underline}**. [The
separation of the vectoralist--hacker class antagonism from the
capitalist--worker antagonism emerges out of the development of the
forces of production]{.underline}, [which generated a]{.underline}n
extensive and intensive [rationalization]{.underline}---
[or]{.underline} better yet, **[abstraction---of the production of
information]{.underline}**. As Adorno and Horkheimer pointed out in
their own synthesis of Marx and Weber, the **[rationalization of means
serves irrational ends]{.underline}**, not least in [treating nature as
a mere thing to be exploited in the same manner as the working
class]{.underline} is exploited, thr[ough the subordination of
everything to the commodity form]{.underline}.30 [Each successive form
of class]{.underline} rule [may be more abstract]{.underline} than those
it subsumes, [but it isn't more rational]{.underline}. [The antagonism
internal to the vectoralist--hacker class relation has all three
components]{.underline} of a class relation: [property, authority, and
expertise]{.underline}. [It emerges]{.underline} in the first instance
[out of a]{.underline} **[rationalization of]{.underline}** so-called
**[intellectual property law]{.underline}**, [which]{.underline}
increasingly [encloses]{.underline} **[information in]{.underline}**
something close to **[a private property right]{.underline}**.
[Vectoralist domination]{.underline} over all subordinate classes [is
sustained by the automation of relations of authority]{.underline},
which take the form of **[pervasive surveillance and
quantification]{.underline}**---a **[rationalization of]{.underline}**
all aspects of **[human activity]{.underline}**. Domination through
expertise turns out to be an interesting and subtle question. The rise
of the vectoralist class changes the kinds of [credentials
that]{.underline} appear to [have value]{.underline} for class power.
These [became increasingly technical]{.underline} in nature. Access to
such qualifications appears to offer the possibility of class mobility.
Here the perspectives of Weber and Durkheim are useful supplements.
[Opportunity hoarding through control of access to elite credentials
sustains social closure]{.underline} and the exercise of occupational
power through expertise. Since both men and women, not to mention women
of color, sometimes have elite credentials in the formal sense, their
exclusion ends up being enforced by more old-fashioned means of
authority and domination, [through the "toxic work
environment]{.underline}." A lot more could be said about that. Here I
simply add the possibility of an additional axis of class antagonism, in
addition to property, authority, and expertise. This is what we might
call [the technical dimension of class antagonism]{.underline}, where it
[is built into the form of the information vector itself]{.underline}.
This has many aspects, from the design of [algorithms determining credit
to]{.underline} the development of [object-oriented programming
environments, which allow]{.underline} for [the rationalization of the
production of component parts of programming by a dispersed and
disempowered hacker class while preserving central control of
proprietary code]{.underline}. Rather than domination or exploitation,
this form of class antagonism emerges out of asymmetries of information
and protocols of selective access and control.31 Forms not only of class
but also of [**gendered and racialized discrimination** have migrated
from relations of property, authority, and expertise and have been
encoded as]{.underline} technical (or [**algorithmic**) forms of
**power**]{.underline}. 32 [Thinking about class antagonism today
might]{.underline} then [require]{.underline} two steps. For the first,
we are indebted to Wright: Durkheim's interest in the moves of the game
and Weber's interest in the rules of the game can be folded into Marx's
larger perspective, on the changing of the game itself. But for the
second step, we are on our own: [in the absence of faith in the leap
into a gamespace without domination and exploitation]{.underline}, [we
have to]{.underline} **[reimagine the possibilities of action for
subordinate classes]{.underline}**. Wright speaks in very measured terms
of the normative aspect of Marx's project. He does not name the trope
toward which its heliotropism tends: Communism. But his analysis of
class rests nonetheless on it as a "hidden god."33 Wright maintains the
faith in the absence rather than the presence of possibility in either
its revolutionary or reformist forms. I think we might have to
**[reimagine the normative goal itself]{.underline}**, [based on the
combined experiences of the farmer, worker, and hacker as subordinate
classes]{.underline}. [What is the just means of making and distributing
matter, energy, and information]{.underline}? That might then inform
strategies and tactics for changing the vectoralist game. But [in the
meantime]{.underline}, [we might have to make do with struggles over the
rules of the existing gamespace]{.underline} and over the everyday lives
of players, hustlers, and grinders making their moves, as the vulgar
blues language of the times---from hip hop to trap---would have it.34
Besides reaching out to those indebted to more classical approaches of
Durkheim and Weber, Wright addresses prominent contemporary social
theorists who try to offer original perspectives. Here I'll take sides
with Wright against some of the most widely known alternative social
theories--- Thomas Piketty, Guy Standing, and Wolfgang Streek---while
introducing their perspectives into the thought experiment that this is
no longer capitalism but something worse. Thomas Piketty deserves credit
for putting inequality back on the agenda as more than a mere problem of
unequal opportunity. 35 His empirical work shows that [the sharp rise in
income of the top 10% is really that of the]{.underline} 1% or even the
**[.1%.]{.underline}** A fair bit of this came from [the rise of **super
salaries** rather than income on capital]{.underline}. The CEO "class"
is setting its own pay. Here I would want to inquire as to how, in a
political economy running on information, the capacity to control (but
not exactly own) the means of production accrues to a class that
presents itself as the celebrities of information control itself.
[**Commanding attention** becomes a form of **class
power**]{.underline}. The technicalities of Piketty's work centers on
the capital:income ratio as a way of measuring the value of capital
relative to total income of economy. As Wright says, "Piketty's basic
argument is that this ratio is the structural basis for the distribution
of income between owners of capital and labor: all other things being
equal, for a given return on capital, the higher this ratio, the higher
the proportion of national income going to wealth holders."36 As growth
declines, the capital:income ratio rises. There's a rise in the weight
of inherited wealth, while concentrations of income also rise. It's the
worst of both worlds: a rentier "class" plus a CEO "class" of
appearance-peddlers carving up the world between them at the expense of
everyone else. Picketty starts out with a class analysis but loses it
once he gets into the empirical work, where he treats CEO income as
return on labor, as most income tables do. Wright: "In the modern
corporation many of the powersof-capital are held by top executives....
They occupy what I have called contradictory locations within class
relations ... They exercise their capitalist-derived power within the
class relations of the firm to appropriate part of the corporation's
profits for their personal accounts."37 But is their power really
"capitalist-derived," or is it now something else? Something like a
joint managing of appearances between those who represent a firm to the
market and the market that is supposed to value it. But [how to value a
company when so much of its asset base takes the form of
information]{.underline}? [A corporation today is among other things a
**brand**, a slew of **patents**, a **logistical process**, a corral of
**expert hackers** turning out new **intellectual
property**]{.underline}. [How can **information** be **turned into
value**, and an **opportunity** to be **hoarded**, when **there
aren't**]{.underline} really **[private languages]{.underline}**, [and
**information is**]{.underline} in principle [a **nonrivalrous
good**]{.underline}?38 Piketty does not separate out real estate from
capital, yet there might be good reasons to do so. Landlords and
capitalists are already different kinds of ruling classes with
overlapping but not identical interests. Ground rent and profit are not
the same kinds of surplus extraction. [Landlords]{.underline},
perversely, may [benefit from the rise of the vector]{.underline} in
ways Capital does not. As Matteo Pasquinelli says, today's
[landlords]{.underline} (often with giant global property portfolios)
[increase their rents by extracting the information value that the
presence of the hacker class produces]{.underline}.39 On the one hand,
attracting so-called creatives or techies to a neighborhood drives out
working class and non-white tenants. On the other hand, the [new
residents add layers of information]{.underline} to the place [that can
be recuperated as value to sell]{.underline} it to bankers and lawyers
and drive out mere hacker class tenants in turn. **[Gentrification is
but a step to aristofication.]{.underline}** One could think further
here about Ricardo's ancient tension between ground rent and profit, but
with the focus shifted from the rural to the urban and the monopoly
rents to be extracted from urban locations.40 Guy Standing is the name
most associated with the now widely discussed idea of the precariat as a
class rather than just a bad life chance.41 He offers a
three-dimensional definition of class, as structured by relations of
production, relations of distribution, and (interestingly) relations to
the state. He identifies seven classes: plutocracy, salariat, proficians
(professional + technician), working class, precariat, unemployed, and
lumpen-precariat. The precariat have insecure jobs. Their sources of
income other than wages are disappearing. They become less citizens of
the state and more like mere denizens. Not only are their jobs
precarious, they are vulnerable within relations of distribution and
marginal to the state. The precariat includes people bumped out of
working class communities and families who experience a relative
deprivation in relation to a real or imagined past. It also includes
migrants and asylum seekers for whom the present is absent. The
precariat increasingly includes people falling out of an educated middle
class---think academic adjunct labor---who lack a future. For Standing
this makes a potentially "dangerous class." Marxists might think of the
precariat as workers who (in Weberian terms) experienced poor life
chances. Standing thinks there are antagonisms between the precariat and
the working class. But do the precariat and workers have distinct
interests? Maybe not.42 Maybe they can share an interest in changing the
game (although one might want to say more here about how workers and the
precariat might have different interests about the rules and moves of
the game). Unionization, for example, can secure some sort of steady
work for the workers in the union, but whether it benefits those outside
of it is an open question. Wolfgang Streeck argues, in a Durkheimian
vein, that capitalism works better when there are constraints on
rational, self-interested action, based on trust, legitimacy, and
responsibility. 43 The wrinkle Wright introduces is to argue that [the
level of **constraint on self-interest** that is **optimal for
capitalists** is **below** that which is **optimal for workers**.
Capital seeks to **remove constraints to augment its power** even **past
the point where these are economically inefficient**]{.underline}.
Wright: "[The zeal to dismantle the regulatory machinery of
capitalism]{.underline} since the early 1980s [was driven by a desire to
**undermine the conditions for empowerment** of interests opposed to
those of capitalists]{.underline}---[**even if doing so meant
under-regulating capitalism** from the point of view of **long-term
needs of capital accumulation.**]{.underline}"44 One could see this a
bit differently by [separating]{.underline} out [the interests of the
capitalist and vectoralist class]{.underline}. [The regulatory
regime]{.underline} emerging in the last quarter century **[favors the
mobility of information]{.underline}**, and not just finance, [as a
means of coordinating economic activity transnationally]{.underline},
[at the expense]{.underline} not just of workers but [of]{.underline}
those forms of [capitalist enterprise tied to physical]{.underline}
plant and [infrastructure]{.underline}, and thus with an interest in
local, regional, or national relations of trust, legitimacy, and
responsibility. We can read Wright's conclusion against the grain:
"**[Enlightenment of the capitalist class to their long-term
interests]{.underline}** in a strong civic culture of obligation and
trust **[is not enough]{.underline}**; **[the balance of
power]{.underline}** also **[needs to be changed]{.underline}**. And
[since this shift]{.underline} in balance of power [will be costly to
those in privileged positions]{.underline}, [it will only occur
through]{.underline} a process of [mobilization and
struggle]{.underline}."45 [What if those capitalists tied
to]{.underline} actually [producing things]{.underline} in a particular
place already [know this, but]{.underline} they have [lost
power]{.underline} [to a]{.underline} quite [different]{.underline} kind
of [ruling class]{.underline}, [which operates at a **higher level of
abstraction**]{.underline}, or in Weberian terms, at a new stage of
rationalization? [They own or control the information about things,
rather than the things themselves]{.underline}. [This is]{.underline}
not inherently more rational, but it is [more abstract]{.underline}, and
hence [more powerful]{.underline}. To imagine new kinds of class
compromise might require a rethink about which classes could compromise.
Since there appears to be no way to change the game, Wright looks to
those who wanted to change the rules within the game, such as Walter

[and worker's cooperatives]{.underline}. [But one has to wonder
**whether such things are**]{.underline} all that
**[viable]{.underline}** (at least as traditionally conceived),
[given]{.underline} that [the]{.underline} forces of production drive
increasingly [abstract relations of production]{.underline}, [which
appear]{.underline} then [as **transnational legal and treaty forms
protecting information as private property**]{.underline}. Trebor Scholz
proposes a form of platform cooperativism as a more contemporary

**counterstack on the infrastructural level**]{.underline}. Wright:
"[Changes in technology]{.underline} may [make the anchoring of
capitalist production in locally rooted]{.underline}, [high
productivity]{.underline} small and medium size [enterprises more
feasible]{.underline}."48 One might call this the Brooklyn-effect, after
the boom in small business, even manufacturing, there.49 But while the
actual products have some connection to locality, such [**localism
relies on an** **information infrastructure** or vector stack **owned
and controlled by the vectoralist class**]{.underline}: [**Google,
Amazon, Paypal**, and so forth all **get their cut**.]{.underline}
[Their power may take the form of a **vectoral
infrastructure**]{.underline} that [enables them to **extract
information asymmetries**]{.underline} [from **both capital and** from
**subordinate classes** and to **accumulate asymmetric information**
about all of these activities now **subordinated to the
vector**]{.underline}. Thus, where Wright says, "I assume that an exit
from capitalism is not an option in the present historical period,"50 I

[this is already not capitalism, but something worse.]{.underline} It's

**[which part of it is real]{.underline}** at all---and perhaps one

[What's less common is to think this]{.underline} **[within a larger

of information asymmetry. Race and gender oppressio]{.underline}n now
[connect to all four dimensions of class]{.underline}. The immediate

[categorize people into clusters]{.underline}. [They are]{.underline}
indeed [things that **the vector of information**]{.underline}

**[white]{.underline}**. **[Class]{.underline}** in the Marxist sense
**[is harder to make palpable]{.underline}**. First, class means

that's like. [One's]{.underline} public [self]{.underline} [is supposed
to be **a hard-charging boss**]{.underline}. As Cardi B. raps, "I'm a
boss you a worker bitch."58 What it means [to be a **boss** is now
**modeled on the vectorialist** rather than the capitalist
class]{.underline}. It's about **[accumulating asymmetric relations of
information]{.underline}**. It is about **[commanding and monopolizing
attention]{.underline}**. It's about **[monetizing
appearances]{.underline}**. [The thing to **aspire to own** is **a
brand**]{.underline}, [starting with **the branded self**]{.underline}
and branching out from there. If this is the public face the subaltern
has to adopt, whether worker or hacker, the private feelings it masks
may be something else altogether. Failure to live up to your own
personal brand is understood through languages that are medical,
therapeutic, or "spiritual."59 [This is a **world of boredom, anxiety,
depression, lack of focus, lack of will**]{.underline}. [It can
take]{.underline} a lot of [pharmaceutical
management]{.underline}---legal and illegal---[to produce the public
face]{.underline} of today. 60 To the extent that there is a language
about power that can address these experiences, [it negotiates
perspectives from critical race theory and feminism]{.underline}, as it
should, [but]{.underline} often **[stops short of a language of
class]{.underline}**. [That language]{.underline}, against which these
others struggled to find room, has [atrophied as vectoral
power]{.underline} [has **subsumed capitalist power**]{.underline} as
its subordinate form. **[The language of class analysis]{.underline}**
(in the Marxist sense) **[appears outdated, because it
is]{.underline}**. [It **no longer includes**]{.underline} **[all
the]{.underline}** **[classes in contention]{.underline}**. [If we think
synchronically about]{.underline} a matrix of [antagonistic classes that
includes emerging ones,]{.underline} then **[capitalism can be returned
to historical thought from its holiday in eternity.]{.underline}**

#### The vector consumes all -- intellectual property allows the extraction of value from the hacker class by commodifying creativity and controlling freedom, pushing the world to extinction.

**Wark 19** (McKenzie Wark, Activist, Writer, PhD in Communications,
Professor at the New School for Social Research and Eugene Lang College,
Culture and Media; Program Director, Gender Studies, 2019, Verso,
\"Capital is dead\", Chapter 5: A Time Machine Theory of
History)//gideon

It is a strange thing, this mode of production. What Bernal and Richta
called [the scientific and technological revolution]{.underline} really
[did happen]{.underline}, and [in the West, not the East. But it was the
product of a]{.underline} weird kind of "[socialism]{.underline}." [It
came out of a]{.underline} **[wartime socialization of scientific and
technical power]{.underline}**. [Scientists and engineers]{.underline},
in academic and corporate laboratories, [**cooperated** with each
other]{.underline}. Their **[innovations weren't immediately patented,
they were shared]{.underline}**. [That laid the groundwork for
postwar]{.underline} developments in the [forces of
production]{.underline}. To some extent this "[socialism"
continued]{.underline}, [under the]{.underline} auspices of the
[Pentagon's Advanced Projects Research Agency]{.underline},
[which]{.underline} among other things [funded key work in
computation]{.underline}.52 If there was [a key innovation that came out
of this]{.underline} strange [western statesocialist
military---industrial complex]{.underline}, it [was **the technics of
information**]{.underline}. It took a while for the pieces to come
together. By the early twenty-first century, the odd thing is that the
[state-socialist sponsored scientific and technical effort]{.underline},
[made]{.underline} first [to defeat the Axis powers and]{.underline}
then to defeat [the Soviets]{.underline}, en[ded up being a way to
compete with Japanese industry]{.underline} abroad [and]{.underline} to
[defeat the working classes]{.underline} at home. [A]{.underline}
basically [**socialized research program** became **the means to
build**]{.underline} an infrastructure---what Benjamin Bratton calls the
stack, what I call **[the vector]{.underline}**---[for **a systematic
and global privatization of objects, subjects, and**]{.underline} the
**[information]{.underline}** in between them.53 [That]{.underline}
**[this was not an inevitable destiny]{.underline}** [of science and
technology]{.underline} [was masked by the **suppression of critical and
dissenting voices** among scientists themselves]{.underline}.
[Bernalism]{.underline}, or the Social Relations of Science movement
more broadly, [was **shut down in** the **red scare politics** of the
Cold War]{.underline}. In [the]{.underline} relative [absence of
that]{.underline} strand of [thinking]{.underline}, the available
[stories]{.underline} for accounting for this historical period have
[lacked]{.underline} a sense of the [class conflicts]{.underline}
internal to these new forces of production [and the extent to which they
were likely to transform capitalism]{.underline}, such as it was in the
late twentieth century, [into something else]{.underline}. [The
story]{.underline} that is [best known about science and technology
during the war is the Manhattan project and the atom bomb]{.underline}.
[But]{.underline} perhaps [it was not the only piece]{.underline} of the
puzzle [that mattered]{.underline}. [The war in the Pacific
was]{.underline} probably [the biggest logistical operation ever
conducted]{.underline} up until that time. Robert
[McNamara]{.underline}, [who would]{.underline} later [run]{.underline}
the [Ford]{.underline} Motor Company and then the Pentagon, [was an
apprentice logistics]{.underline} [expert]{.underline} during the war.
[These were pioneering efforts to control]{.underline} the movement and
combination of incredibly [complex arrays of resources]{.underline}
across vast territories [using communication and
computation]{.underline}.54 [What started]{.underline} out [as the means
to beat the Axis powers]{.underline}, and then contain the Soviets, and
then to compete with Japanese industry, [was]{.underline} in the end
[the means to **globalize production**]{.underline}, [**exploit**
the]{.underline} newly available **[cheap labor of]{.underline}** the
People's Republic of **[China]{.underline}**, [and
**destroy**]{.underline} the power of **[organized labor]{.underline}**
within Italy, the United States, and [throughout]{.underline} much of
[the overdeveloped world]{.underline}. But there's a paradox attendant
to this. C[apital thought it was using]{.underline} some
[new]{.underline} kinds of [communication and computational power in its
struggle with labor, but]{.underline} in the end [the **capitalist
class** too ended up being **subsumed under that power**]{.underline}.
The capitalist class became a [subsidiary]{.underline} ruling class [to
the vectoralist class]{.underline}. **[Capital is dead; the Vector
lives]{.underline}**. [A capitalist class owns the means of
production]{.underline}, the means of organizing labor. **[A vectoralist
class owns the means of organizing the means of
production]{.underline}**. [The vector has a double form]{.underline}:
the form of vector [along which information is to be routed]{.underline}
(**[the extensive vector]{.underline}**), [and]{.underline} the form of
the vector [along which information can be stored and
computed]{.underline} (**[the intensive vector]{.underline}**). [A
vectoralist class]{.underline} also [owns and **controls the production
process** through **patents, copyrights, brands, trademarks, proprietary
logistical processes**]{.underline}, and the like. It is curious that if
one looks at the world's biggest [corporations]{.underline} these days,
a lot of their [power and property is in vectoral form]{.underline}.
[Many]{.underline} of them **[don't]{.underline}** actually **[make the
things they sell]{.underline}**. [They **control the production process
by owning and controlling the information**]{.underline}. Even when they
do still make the stuff, a quite remarkable amount of the
[valuation]{.underline} of the company [comes from portfolios of

more abstract form of technical power]{.underline}. When considering the

[it seems to be able to extract value]{.underline} not just from labor
but [from]{.underline} what Tiziana Terranova calls **[free
labor]{.underline}**. 55 Even when you just stroll down the street, [the
phone]{.underline} in your purse or pocket [is reporting
data]{.underline} back [to some vectoralist entity]{.underline}. The
vectoralist class seems to be able to extract revenue out of qualitative
information in much the same way as banks extract it out of quantitative
information. Perhaps the exercise of power through control of
quantitative and qualitative information is characteristic of the same
ruling class. Second, [the vectoralist class subordinates]{.underline}
the old kind of ruling class, [a capitalist class]{.underline}, in the

subjected rural production to commodi-fication through ground rent. In
that sense, [the rise of a vectoralist]{.underline} class
[is]{.underline} a [similar]{.underline} and subsequent development
[within intra-ruling class dynamics]{.underline}. [The vectoralist class
still sits atop a pyramid of exploited labor]{.underline},
[but]{.underline} it [depends]{.underline} also [on extracting a surplus
out of another]{.underline}, fairly [privileged but]{.underline} still
[subordinate]{.underline} class. I call it the **[hacker

[embedded in the design of the interface for the **creative

[**information**]{.underline} in the world **[into

In short, a new class dynamic, between vectoralist and hacker, was added
to an already complex pattern of relations between dominant and

rise of the vectoralist class]{.underline}. [But]{.underline} it was
**[the state form of the former East that has prevailed in the former
West.]{.underline}** [**The vector** is]{.underline} not just a means of
transforming production. It is also [a way of **transforming state

[model]{.underline} worldwide [uses the vector to **realize the dreams
of the KGB**]{.underline} of old, an information state. This is what Guy
Debord called [the]{.underline} stage of the [integrated]{.underline}
[spectacle]{.underline}, **[combining the worst of the former East and
West]{.underline}**.57 [The West is now **the former
West**]{.underline}. [Its economy became something else]{.underline}.
**[It isn't capitalism any more---it's worse]{.underline}**. [It
**takes**]{.underline} even more **[control away from]{.underline}**
work **[life]{.underline}** and everyday life. [It
**expands**]{.underline} the **[exploitation of nature to]{.underline}**
possible **[extinction]{.underline}**. [It is]{.underline} certainly
[not]{.underline} the wonderful dream of [a "postindustrial
society]{.underline}," still less Bernal and Richta's [accelerationist
socialism]{.underline}. [It is a]{.underline} relatively [new
and]{.underline} more [elaborate]{.underline} form of [class
domination]{.underline}, one in more or less "peaceful coexistence" with
the Russian former East, whose global significance is reduced to that of
predatory oligarchy monopolizing a resource export economy. 58 The
Soviet Union paid a high price for not figuring out the role of
information and reaching a modus vivendi with its scientific workers.

#### We advocate for Détournment and strategizing, the return of subversive qualities to congealed and analyzed texts; labor cannot become ideological. We must generate novel revolutionary strategies for our time

**Wark 19** (McKenzie Wark, Activist, Writer, PhD in Communications,
Professor at the New School for Social Research and Eugene Lang College,
Culture and Media; Program Director, Gender Studies, 2019, Verso,
\"Capital is dead\", Chapter 1: The Sublime Language of My
Century)//gideon

All of this takes as a given the transmission of Marx common to
nonMarxist and even post-Marxist philosophers and other humanities or
social science scholars and the not very different approach of rather
scholastic party functionaries of Marxism's "classical" period.48 There
are other readers of Marx, and some of them are poets, or who read as
poets do. [Modern poets]{.underline}, [less interested in the meaning of
the texts]{.underline} (the always deferred signified) [than in the
signs themselves]{.underline} (the materiality of the signifier).49 [One
that has been of particular use]{.underline} to me [is]{.underline}
something that is much less a method of reading and more a procedure for
writing: [what Guy Debord called **détournement**]{.underline}.50 The
word includes the sense of the detour, [the turning aside]{.underline},
a hijacking [but also a seduction]{.underline}. Debord: "[The device of
détournement **restores**]{.underline} all [their **subversive qualities
to past critical judgments that have congealed into respectable
truths**]{.underline} ... The defining characteristic of this use of
[détournement is]{.underline} the [necessity for distance to be
maintained toward whatever has been turned into an official
verity]{.underline} ... Ideas improve. The meaning of words has a part
in this improvement. [Plagiarism is necessary]{.underline}, [progress
implies it]{.underline}. Staying close to an author's phrasing,
plagiarism exploits his expressions, erases false ideas, replaces them
with correct ideas ... [Détournement is the antithesis of
quotation]{.underline}, [of a theoretical authority]{.underline}
invariably [tainted if only because it has become quotable]{.underline},
[because it is now a fragment torn away from its context, from its own
movement]{.underline} ... [Détournement is]{.underline}, by contrast,
[the fluid language of anti-ideology]{.underline} ... Détournement
founds its cause on [nothing but its own truth as critique at work in
the present]{.underline}."51 [Debord's writing]{.underline} itself [is
a]{.underline} brilliant détou[rnement of Marx and
Lautréamont]{.underline} (and much else), one [that generated a
style]{.underline} (and some fresh concepts) [for]{.underline}
understanding [the historical moment of the mid-twentieth
century]{.underline}. Marx: "The wealth of those societies in which the
capitalist mode of production prevails, presents itself as an immense
accumulation of commodities ..." Debord: "The whole life of those
societies in which modern conditions of production prevail presents
itself as an immense accumulation of spectacles."52 And so, once more,
comrades, [if we would become critics of our times!]{.underline} Let's
[try some more détournement to **produce**]{.underline} some
[**different language** out of that which comes down to us, **rather
than trying to interpret the eternal essence of the text as if we could
reproduce it as more of the same**]{.underline}. To practice the style
of [negation today requires the negation of some old
styles]{.underline}. But how do we broach the question of style in Marx?
For Keston Sutherland Capital needs readers rather than "curators of
concepts."53 [Capital is written in clashing styles, aimed at a
readership Marx knew to be divided by class]{.underline}. [To the
bourgeois]{.underline} reader, aping genteel sensibilities, [Marx
addresses himself as a satirist]{.underline}, writing at the expense of
the myths the bourgeois lives by. For instance, Sutherland claims that
Marx's famous overture on the fetish character of the commodities has
been "influentially mistranslated" in accounts that try to master the
text by extracting its concepts.54 [Commodity fetishism is not a
misapprehension of the commodity]{.underline}. 55 Marx is saying
something about the making of the commodity itself. Human labor is not
just abstracted into a homogenous quantity in the commodity form. [Labor
gets minced and boiled into]{.underline} Gallerte: aspic, meat jelly. Or
in today's terms into something like what appears in those truly
disgusting online videos that show the extrusion from some machine of
that major ingredient of hamburgers: [pink goo.]{.underline} Sutherland:
"[The living hands, muscles and nerves of the wage laborer are mere
'animal substances,' ingredients for the feast of the
capitalist]{.underline}."56 [Marx's]{.underline} image of what happens
to **[labor is not a genteel conceptual abstraction but a vulgar image
from industrial butchery.]{.underline}** "[The object of Marx's
satire]{.underline} on abstract human labor [is not the worker reduced
to a condiment but the bourgeois consumer who eats him for
breakfast]{.underline}."57 [Capital is "a work of
sustained]{.underline}, aggressively [satirical détournement in which
the risks and failures of style are arguments in themselves, irreducible
to theoretical proposition.]{.underline}"58 Elsewhere, Marx détourns
phrases from Dante, Goethe, and Shakespeare, erasing false ideas,
replacing them with correct ones. [The fetish character of commodities
is a détournement of a work of racist ethnography by Charles De
Brosse]{.underline}.59 [In]{.underline} the [De Brosse]{.underline}
source text, [the]{.underline} genteel and [enlightened reader
is]{.underline} first [astonished that]{.underline} stupid
"[savages]{.underline}" [worship fetishes, but disciplines
this]{.underline} astonishment [into knowledge]{.underline}. [In
Marx]{.underline} it is the reverse. [The commodity appears]{.underline}
at first as something [rational]{.underline} and known to the genteel
sensibility, [but on closer inspection is]{.underline} quite
[astonishing]{.underline}. It is [we]{.underline}, gentle reader, who
[are stupid before the fetish]{.underline}. There is no reconciliation
to this strange thing. [It has to be abolished]{.underline}. To write
after Marx is not to claim a genteel mastery of concepts alone. Where I
would press on (which Sutherland very likely wouldn't) is to suggest
that [one way to restore]{.underline} a certain [vulgar energy to
writing might be to take]{.underline} Marx's tactics of [détournement
and apply them to the concepts of eternal Capital]{.underline} that have
been extracted from Capital itself [in]{.underline} certain [genteel
readings and perpetuated as a kind of myth]{.underline}. The truth of
the matter is that **[Marxist writing itself became
ideological]{.underline}**. Its acquiescence to the sense of capitalism
being eternal is one sure sign of this. **[Hence the necessity of the
gesture, the thought experiment, of declaring]{.underline}**: **[Capital
is dead]{.underline}**. It is dead [like God before it]{.underline}, and
as with that discovery**, [to announce this is treated in the
"marketplace of ideas" as madness]{.underline}**. The corpus of [Marx is
read within a textology of transmission]{.underline},
[using]{.underline} scholastic [protocols of quotation, exegesis, and
interpretation descended from]{.underline} those developed for
[religious texts]{.underline}.60 And so not surprisingly **[Marxism
became a minor form of (protestant!) religion]{.underline}**---one of
the boring ones, with long sermons and much commentary on scripture.
[**To interrupt these habits** requires **not another reading of Marx,**
promising to peel away the false and reveal the true
essence]{.underline}. Rather, **[it takes another style of
writing]{.underline}**. [Détournement does not care about]{.underline}
the [self-identity of the textual corpus or the eternal
spirit]{.underline} hidden [within]{.underline}. [It takes what it finds
useful]{.underline} or amusing [for]{.underline} composing the textual
expression of **[the present situation]{.underline}**. [Judged **in
relation to the sacred scriptures it will**]{.underline} of course
**[appear as heretical, mad, wrong, or vulgar]{.underline}.** This is a
poetics that intends to differ from the material it appropriates.
[Détournement is no]{.underline} [respecter of private property or
public propriety]{.underline}. [It has no interest in those who claim
Marx]{.underline} ([or]{.underline} for that matter
[Debord]{.underline}) [as their patrimony]{.underline}, as the field
they alone are warranted or patented to cultivate and trade. [Our
task]{.underline}, in the thought experiments gathered here[, is to
appropriate from the Marxist tradition for the composition
of]{.underline} frankly Frankensteinian [monster-texts whose only
interest is in being **anti-ideological tactics**]{.underline}, in
[pointing]{.underline} from within the combinatory of terms [to the
**limits of**]{.underline} what Flaubert called **[received
ideas]{.underline}**.61 There's not much choice but to work with
received ideas, but th[ere's more than one way to select from
tradition.]{.underline} So let's think about the present on these terms:
[what if,]{.underline} rather than start at the beginning, [one started
at the end]{.underline}? The **[capitalism story always starts in the
past]{.underline}**, with the birth of capitalism, [**and imagines
a**]{.underline} destiny, a **[teleology]{.underline}**, **[wherein the
present must be some continuum from that past]{.underline}**.62 [This
must be some modification of the essence of the thing]{.underline}.
Let's do it the other way around. **[Let's first describe the
present]{.underline}, [then]{.underline}** secondarily **[figure out
where it came from]{.underline}**. This may even, in the end, involve
modifying our understanding of capitalism's pasts. [Any attempt to
describe the present in its own language is]{.underline} more than
[likely to end up reproducing the language of its ruling
class]{.underline} at best, or at worst the left-over language of
obsolete ruling classes. [Hence]{.underline} the method of
[détournement]{.underline}, [appropriating received ideas,
but]{.underline} also [erasing and correcting]{.underline}. Let's [pick
a Marx text to détourn. Rather than start where Marx]{.underline} more
or less [ended]{.underline}, [with Capital]{.underline}, let's [start
where his "mature" work]{.underline} began, with the Preface to the
Contribution to the Critique of Political Economy. 63 [Let's **start not
with capitalism**, as if we could just assume that is what this still
is]{.underline}. Let's **[start with]{.underline}** Marx's sketch of
**[how to think about modes of production]{.underline}**. I have only
modified it slightly. [In]{.underline} the [social-technical
production]{.underline} of their existence, [humans]{.underline}
inevitably [enter into definite relations]{.underline}, which are
[independent of their desires]{.underline}, namely [relations of
production]{.underline} appropriate to a given stage in the development
of their material forces of production (and reproduction). [**The
totality of** these **relations of production constitutes the economic
structure of society**, the infrastructure, **on which arises a legal,
political and cultural superstructure.**]{.underline} The mode of
production of material life conditions the general process of social,
political, and cultural life. It is not the ideologies of humans that
determine their social-technical existence, but [their
**social-technical existence**]{.underline} that [**determines their
ideologies**. Accidents happen in]{.underline} the course of [historical
development]{.underline}. [The forces of production come into conflict
with]{.underline} the [existing relations of production]{.underline}
or--- this just says the same thing in legal terms---with the property
relations within the framework of which they have operated hitherto.
From forms for the development of the productive forces, [these
relations turn into their fetters]{.underline}. [Then
begins]{.underline} an era of [transformation of]{.underline} the
[superstructures]{.underline}. The [changes in the]{.underline} forms of
[social-technical metabolism lead]{.underline} sooner or later [to the
transformation of the]{.underline} whole immense
[superstructure]{.underline}. In studying such transformations, [it
is]{.underline} always [hard to distinguish between]{.underline} the
[material transformation]{.underline} of the conditions of production,
which can be determined with the methods of a social science, [and
the]{.underline} legal, political, religious, artistic, or
philosophic---in short, the [mythic or ideological forms]{.underline} in
which humans sense and feel this conflict and fight it out. [Just as one
does not judge an individual by a Facebook profile]{.underline}, so [one
cannot judge]{.underline} such a period of [transformation by its
myths]{.underline}. On the contrary, [these myths must be explained from
the contradictions of material life]{.underline}, from the
[conflict]{.underline} existing [between the social-technical forces of
production and the relations of production]{.underline}. [No social
order is]{.underline} ever [destroyed before all the productive
forces]{.underline} for which it is sufficient [have been
developed]{.underline}, [and]{.underline} more [abstract]{.underline}
relations of [production never replace older ones before the material
conditions]{.underline} for their existence [have matured]{.underline}
within the framework of the old society. [Social-technical]{.underline}
forms of [organization]{.underline} thus usually [set]{.underline}
themselves [only]{.underline} such [tasks]{.underline} as [they are able
to solve]{.underline}, [since]{.underline} closer examination will
always show that **[the problem itself arises only when the material
conditions for its solution are already present]{.underline}** or at
least in the course of formation. In broad outline, [the ancient,
feudal, despotic, capitalist, and vectoralist modes of production may be
designated as **epochs**]{.underline} [marking]{.underline} the
extension of [the exploitation of nature by]{.underline}
social-technical forms of **[increasing abstraction]{.underline}.** [The
capitalist mode of production was imagined to be **the last antagonistic
form of the social process of production**.]{.underline}
**[Marx]{.underline}** [thought]{.underline} that "[the prehistory of
human society]{.underline} accordingly [closes with this social
formation]{.underline}."64 On that, [he **was mistaken**]{.underline}.

#### We advocate for Vulgar Marxism: a renegade language; a decentralized stack that avoids the drive to accumulate information asymmetries; the every-day life of Andrey Platonov, the blues of Angela Davis, the cinema of Pier Paolo Pasolini, and the art of Asger Jorn -- the aesthetics of vulgar reality

**Wark 19** (McKenzie Wark, Activist, Writer, PhD in Communications,
Professor at the New School for Social Research and Eugene Lang College,
Culture and Media; Program Director, Gender Studies, 2019, Verso,
\"Capital is dead\", Chapter 7: Four Cheers for Vulgarity!!!!)//gideon

As a way of counterprogramming against genteel Marxism, I want to look
at some peculiar instances of the vulgar kind: two about the twenties,
two from the sixties. Andrey Platonov (who was that rare thing, the
great modernist writer with proletarian origins) wrote a masterpiece,
Chevengur, which can be read as many things.22 My attention here is to
its vulgar Marxist side. It's an allegorical counter-history of the
Soviet Union from the October Revolution through the civil war until the
New Economic Policy, but seen from the points of view of characters who
are not even proletarian. They are orphans. This is not history from
below but history from below the below. Chevengur does not present the
October Revolution from the point of view of the edicts issued from the
center, but from their noisy, incoherent reception in the provinces.
[Platonov's characters perform]{.underline} their own
[détournement]{.underline} [of Soviet Marx-speak]{.underline}. Far from
revolution as the figurative locomotive of history, actual locomotives
collide head-on due to confused signaling. This world is not in
transition between modes of production as there is hardly any production
at all. There is hardly a working class in Platonov, but there are
comrades. The [comrades]{.underline} are those who [face the same
dangers]{.underline}, [the same exposure to the relentless,
disorganizing inertia of exposure to the world]{.underline}.23 [Humans
and machines, plants and animals can all be comrades]{.underline}. [All
wear away into nothingness in time. The revolution is supposed to
harness all these energies, organize them, inform them, and in the
process render them productive]{.underline}. [But]{.underline} the
tension in Platonov is that [hardship and poverty first make
comrades]{.underline}. [Safety and surplus feed the soul and stimulate
private demands]{.underline}. [The problem is to restore comradeship
beyond the minimal threshold]{.underline} of survival and scarcity.
There [can be no end of history]{.underline} in Platonov's world,
[because nature never lets up]{.underline}, [is never
conquered]{.underline}, is never providence. [Time wears everything
away]{.underline}. [**Communism is**]{.underline} always and **[only a
horizon]{.underline}**, a minimal line [between a blank sky and an empty
land]{.underline}. [Platonov's]{.underline} [characters live on through
**secondary ideas**]{.underline}, which can be made actual in the here
and now. 24 They work on [**food security** or]{.underline} on
**[irrigation]{.underline}**, as Platonov did himself during the famine
years of the civil war. Platonov sticks close to the point of view of
those whose work it is to hoe the fields, to run the railways, those who
find their own ways to be comrades. [Platonov's vulgar Marxism
is]{.underline} neither total revolutionary leap nor social democratic
gradualism. It's **[a practice of everyday life]{.underline}.** The
movement between genteel and vulgar Marxism plays out strongly in the
work of [Angela Davis.]{.underline} She studied philosophy with Herbert
Marcuse in the sixties but was also a militant in the Black Liberation
Movement. Davis: "If I still retained any of the elitism which almost
inevitably insinuates itself into the minds of college students, I lost
it all in the course of the \[Black Panther Party\] political education
sessions."25 I want to focus on her study of Black women blues singers
of the twenties.26 What she [hears]{.underline} in the recordings of Ma
Rainey and Bessie Smith is [a **Black working class
sensibility**]{.underline}, [appearing through fissures within
patriarchal language]{.underline}. Black working class culture had
little access to writing and publishing, but [through its blues singers
it did find a way to leave a recorded]{.underline} trace of its oral
[language]{.underline}, [even if at the time few heard it outside of
Black proletarian culture]{.underline}. Davis: "As music entered its age
of mechanical reproduction, blues were deemed reproducible only within
the cultural borders of their site of origin."27 [Slave
society]{.underline} had [controlled sexual relations between Black
people]{.underline}. The [abolition]{.underline} of slavery
[revolutionized Black]{.underline} personal [relationships]{.underline}.
[Questions of Black sexuality could not be addressed
through]{.underline} [musical forms of]{.underline} the
[slavery]{.underline} era. Its spirituals invoked a possible world of
collective redemption, at once otherworldly and temporal. It was sacred
universe, all-embracing, an imagined community of hope. It was less
religion as the opium of the people, and more the heart of a heartless
world, to give two of Marx's alternate formulations (the first a
détournement from Heine).28 Out of the frustrated hopes of emancipation
came a more exclusively upward-looking redemption in the form of gospel
music and a lowly, earthy one, in the blues. God and the Devil found
their separate forms, with the Devil having dominion over matters of
love and sex. It was not the secular nature of the blues that drew
church ire, but their sacred quality. [**Blues** women created a space
to **preach about sexuality outside of male-dominated** church
**culture**]{.underline}. In the blues, love is not idealized. Freely
chosen sexual love is a mediation between emancipation from slavery and
new forms of class oppression. Very little in the blues is about
marriage and domesticity. [Blues women were disinterested in the cult of
motherhood and **deal frankly** with **abuse and
abandonment**]{.underline}. [They announce female desire, and it crosses
the public--private distinction. They affirm an emotional community and
Black humanity. They are frank about **lesbian and gay
existence**]{.underline}. [The blues are]{.underline} not a politics,

movement**]{.underline} to which her own lifelong activism belongs.
[They anticipate the feminist principle]{.underline} that the personal

women and prefer men who work to parasitic ones. [And if all else fails,

prison. [They are the music of those]{.underline} among the
[subordinate]{.underline} classes who experience the repressive state

contested black bourgeois notions of 'high' culture that belittled
